US Labor Unrest Surges, Recovery Encounters Many Obstacles

Roosevelt Likely to Intervene

(New York) Recently, the monetary issue in the United States has become increasingly complex, and the labor disputes that have sprung up everywhere are showing signs of further expansion. These two factors seem to have a significant impact on the success of President Roosevelt's recovery plan. The anxiety of various advisors to the US government has become increasingly difficult to conceal recently. (Havas, 29th)

(New York) As labor unrest gradually spreads to many places, a portion of the striking coal miners took actions today that were quite unstable. At the Carnegie Steel plant in Clairborne, Pennsylvania, which employs 6,000 workers, 5,000 striking miners came to harass them, tearing the clothes of some of the factory workers, snatching food from the lunch boxes they carried, and inducing them to join the strike. The anthracite industry in Pennsylvania and Virginia is now almost completely shut down. Strikers at the Chrysler car plant of Ford Company are now threatening to go to Dearborn to prevent work at the Ford factory there. Meanwhile, 400 workers at the Ford factory in Richmond, California, are planning a sympathy strike. The Governor of Pennsylvania today flew to Hyde Park to ask President Roosevelt to intervene as soon as possible, so as to prevent the labor unrest from reaching a level that endangers the national recovery movement. There has been no indication from Hyde Park or Washington yet, but there is considerable activity behind the scenes. It is rumored that President Roosevelt will make an appeal for economic peace to the world with a posture that is more moving than peaceful requests on military preparedness. William Green, President of the American Federation of Labor, claimed that the Federation has increased its membership by 1.5 million in the past three months, and that all the funds used by the Federation for labor matters have also increased as a result. The union plans to request from the National Recovery Administration and Congress a provision in the industry codes stipulating a 30-hour work week. President Green made this statement while the Recovery Administration is considering the possibility of temporarily not implementing the current new standards for wages and working hours for the construction industry and similar industries. However, Green's demand for a 30-hour work week clearly expresses the union's absolute opposition to the Recovery Administration's current plan to postpone the implementation of the new standards. The Recovery Administration is paying attention to this difficult problem, but also stated that the final decision will be made after General Johnson considers it. Green notified the metal industry workers that the industry has not been quick enough to hire more workers as required by the situation, and that the only remedy now is to have six-hour days and five-day weeks. (Reuters, 29th)

Metallurgical and Mining Agreement Approved

(Washington) President Roosevelt approved an agreement between the coal mine employers and employees of the metallurgical industry. According to the agreement, the employers agree to grant employees working conditions that are as favorable as those stipulated in the anthracite industry code. After the approval of this agreement, President Roosevelt hopes that the 75,000 miners currently on strike in Pennsylvania can resume work on Monday. (Havas, 30th)

Currency Declaration to be Released Soon

(Washington) President Roosevelt is about to issue a currency declaration. According to sources in high places, the declaration will include currency devaluation, currency value stabilization, and a promise to restore the gold standard. According to a New York Times report today, President Roosevelt's reason for issuing this declaration is that the recovery movement has reached an important stage, and difficulties have arisen in the rural and public works offices. Recent news shows that production and distribution are both sluggish, and the number of people gaining employment and wage increases is half offset by the reduction in working hours and the rise in the cost of living. (Reuters, 30th)

Russian Aviators Successfully Ascend to Stratosphere in Balloon

19,000 Meters Above Ground

Breaks Professor Piccard's Record

Reuters Moscow, 30th - The Soviet balloon "USSR" initially failed to ascend earlier this week but has now ascended safely today. If its instruments are accurate and reliable, it has ascended to 19,000 meters (11 miles and 7/8 of a mile in height), breaking Professor Piccard's record of 16,201 meters. According to the balloon's pilot, who sent a wireless message from the air, the crew members are in good spirits and all instruments are functioning effectively. This ascent is not intended to break Piccard's record, but to conduct scientific tests in the stratosphere.

Dispute Over Expulsion of German Journalists by Russia

German Government Issues Verbal Note

Considers Russia's Action Unwise

National Daily, Berlin, 29th - Regarding the recent expulsion of German journalists residing in Soviet Russia by the Soviet authorities, the German government today sent a verbal note to the Soviet government, detailing the circumstances and stating that, after careful consideration of all the circumstances, the German Foreign Office cannot consider the expulsion of the German journalists by the Soviet government to be justified, as the incident originated from a very minor matter caused by a mistake on the part of a Soviet journalist. The incident was caused by Mrs. Keyes, a reporter for the TASS news agency, who went to Leipzig to cover the Reichstag fire trial without completing certain procedures and was mistakenly arrested, but was released after a brief interrogation, and the German authorities expressed their apologies. The Soviet authorities considered this an intentional insult and, in retaliation, ordered the expulsion of all German journalists stationed in Moscow. Furthermore, the verbal note issued by the German government stated, "From the perspective of news experts, Russia's expulsion of German journalists is unwise, as it appears to have hindered future friendship between the two countries, and the Soviet Union should bear full responsibility for this."

Six Principles Decided for Relieving Wheat Sales Problems

President Wang Approves and Submits to Various Departments for Handling

(Nanjing) The relief measures for wheat sales problems have been decided by the joint consultation of five agencies, with six relief principles: 1. Increase import tariffs on rice, wheat, and flour, and levy dumping taxes on flour. 2. Strictly prohibit all unreasonable grain taxes and levies in various localities. 3. Make every effort to reduce railway freight rates for wheat and flour. 4. Investigate the proportion of domestic and foreign wheat used by the flour industry nationwide. 5. Regarding the import of American wheat, which affects the sluggish sales of domestic wheat, pay careful attention to such news in the future. 6. Order local governments in various places to make every effort to formulate fair measures to reduce the burden on farmers regarding the fees for grain shops, brokers, and brokers. These principles have been approved by President Wang. Items 1, 2, 4, and 5 are to be handled by the Ministry of Finance. Item 3 is to be handled by the Ministry of Railways and reported back. Item 6 is to be handled by the Ministry of Industry to draft a circular order, and then the Executive Yuan will issue an order to all provincial and municipal governments to comply with it, and each agency will be required to complete it within a time limit. (Special Dispatch, 30th)

Shandong Provincial Government Plans to Establish Security Committee

Expand Security Force

(Jinan) The provincial government, in order to save money due to the severe floods in the province and to cultivate local strength, ordered the Civil Affairs Department to draft a plan. The Civil Affairs Department plans to merge the public security bureaus, militia regiments, and village associations of various counties into a security force, establish a security committee to supervise everything, and set up public self-defense training classes to train personnel, imitating the experimental county and district methods of Heze. The security force will have one large brigade for every dozens of counties and one or several platoons for each county. Li Yizhi Arrives in Xi'an

Upper Reaches to Start with Guiding the Wei River

(Xi'an) Li Yizhi, Chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, arrived in the province from Tongguan on the 29th. The Central News Agency reporter paid a special visit. According to him, the Yellow River Conservancy Commission has closed and the commissioners have taken office. He went to Tianjin, Jinan, Zhengzhou, and Kaifeng to inspect the Yellow River and deeply felt that the cause of the floods was that the embankments along the river had been in disrepair for many years, resulting in a great disaster. In the future, he should actively repair them. The current water situation has returned to normal. The Yellow River Flood Relief Committee is responsible for the two tasks of blocking the breach and post-disaster relief. As for the surveying team organized in Tianjin, it has now set off. The address of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission will be set up in Xi'an. At present, because there is more work downstream, all office personnel are stationed in Kaifeng, under the leadership of Secretary-General Zhang Hanying. As for the upper reaches, it must start with guiding the Wei River. Guiding the Wei River is to seek the interests of some farmers, and governing the Wei River is the first step in governing the Yellow River. The Wei River survey can start on October 1. He will be responsible for the director of the Wei River Guidance Project Office. He is now forming the Wei River Guidance Project Office in Xi'an to start work. As for himself, he is seriously ill and plans to recuperate for three months. When he recovers, he will perform his duties as usual. (Central News Agency, 30th)

Campaign Against Reds in Southern Jiangxi Conducted in Three Routes

Xiong Shihui Talks to Reuters Reporter

(Nanchang) Today, Xiong Shihui, Chairman of Jiangxi Province, told a special reporter from Reuters that he is currently carrying out the campaign against the Reds in southern Jiangxi in three routes: one is road construction, the second is the construction of fortresses, and the third is the reorganization of rural areas. The highway between Nanfeng and Ji'an has now been built, and the road is protected by fortresses along the way wherever it approaches the bandit areas, so it is very safe. All villages and towns with more than 200 households have organized self-defense militias and set up fortresses to prevent the bandits from attacking. There are telephones between villages and cities to communicate news. In the event of a bandit alert, the entire city's militia can be dispatched at any time. Since the abolition of the Likin tax, farmers' taxes have suddenly increased. Jiangxi Province is now implementing a kind of goods tax, dividing various goods into agricultural materials, products, and luxury goods, and levying taxes separately. In this way, the burden on farmers can be slightly reduced. At the same time, Jiangxi Province is implementing a new tax collection law, in which the people automatically submit their taxes directly to the county magistrate without going through tax collectors. Xiong continued to say that he intends to compile a household registration book for Jiangxi Province. Two counties have already started compiling it. Three rural normal schools have been opened a few days ago, with a total of 200 students. Everyone is able to practice in the countryside as a practical exercise. Cooperatives have been established in 300 locations across Jiangxi Province to benefit farmers. These cooperatives borrow money from the Jiangxi branch of the Farmers Bank of China, which is run by Chairman Chiang, at an interest rate of 8% for opening up wasteland and building embankments along Poyang Lake, implementing the method of providing work instead of relief. Regarding the suppression of the Communists, Xiong said that Chairman Chiang is confident that he can eliminate the Communists in southern Jiangxi before Christmas this year. Once the remaining bandits are eliminated, the Jiangxi authorities will form an immigration committee to be responsible for immigrating to the recovered areas. Xiong also said that the Provincial Department of Education is working on editing new textbooks for the purpose of educating residents in the bandit areas, because these farmers have been influenced by the Red bandits for a long time and it is inevitable that their thinking has deteriorated, so it is necessary to correct their ideological errors and use the correct teachings of Confucius to awaken the farmers. (Reuters, 29th)

After the second year of the Republic, the Party's morality declined day by day, the Party's discipline relaxed day by day, and the Party's goals gradually became blurred, so the revolution failed. German Traffic Police's Ancient Roman Salute

Turns Into a Joke

Drivers Mistake It for a Stop Order

Causing Traffic Jams

Havas Berlin dispatch on the 30th: The German government has issued an order requiring all civil servants in the country to perform German-style etiquette, that is, the ancient Roman-style salute of raising the hand to the forehead. The impact of this order has been unexpected. Because when traffic police in the thoroughfares perform this salute, drivers often mistake it for a stop order, which often causes traffic jams. The Prussian Minister of the Interior, in view of this, has prohibited traffic police from performing German or non-German salutes in order to avoid the above situation from happening again.

The Current State of the Japanese Aviation Industry in the Eyes of an American

-How Will Our Countrymen Rise Up and Strive to Compete With Them?-

Recently, the United States has paid close attention to the strengthening of Japanese military preparations. Recently, a certain magazine published an article on the current state of the Japanese Air Force, which was translated by a Japanese person, Yamamuro Sei, and published in the Nagoya Shimbun. It is now translated from the Nagoya Shimbun below to clarify a glimpse of the contents of Japanese aviation.

General Billy Mitchell once said that Japan's absorption of world civilization was all guided by Americans, which is why it has the current state of the aviation industry. It is recalled that Japan first had a hot air balloon in 1892. In 1909, Charles K. Hamilton had an airship soaring in the sky over Tokyo. In 1911, Mr. Mars publicly flew aircraft in various parts of Japan, which aroused the attention of the people of Japan and promoted the motivation for the development of the Japanese aviation industry. Following Mars, was the American W.B. Side Air, who used seaplanes to guide mail transportation between Tokyo and Yokohama. In 1916, the Americans Smith and Nalas held stunt flights, and the Japanese people were even more surprised and had a major impulse, which opened the way for the development of the Japanese aviation industry.

The Strength of the Air Force

In the 1933 fiscal year, the Japanese Army had eight flight regiments, each regiment owning 800 excellent aircraft. The Navy had 450 seaplanes and 350 carrier-based aircraft, totaling approximately 1,450 aircraft. Other civil aviation routes are extended year by year and have been connected with Manchuria. And Japan's current aircraft production, about nine-tenths are domestically produced. Foreign aircraft are gradually decreasing. American-made aircraft and engines have also gradually been driven out by Japan. The Japanese Army and Navy hardly use American-made materials. However, the Japan Air Transport Company, which transports mail and passengers, still has some Fokker-Spars, and Le Rhône-Besson engines. However, these engines will also be replaced by Japanese-made ones. The Japanese factories were initially designed by foreign countries, such as Nieuport (note that the system is the French name Nieuport, invented by the Frenchman Edward, the so-called (Edward Nieuport), Salomon, Grosta and other aircraft, all custom-made from foreign countries. In recent years, the Japanese have imitated various types of aircraft. Japanese-produced aircraft for the Army and Navy have accounted for eight-tenths of the total. The aircraft industry has now entered the era of metal structure. The new first-class machinery is mostly made of aluminum alloy, such as the Nakajima Type 90 fighter, the Kawasaki Type 92 fighter, the Kawasaki Type 88 reconnaissance and bomber), the Mitsubishi reconnaissance aircraft, the Nakajima Type 90 carrier-based fighter, and the Kawanishi Type 90 seaplane reconnaissance aircraft (the numbers of various styles indicate the year in which they were successfully produced. The Japanese calendar year 2592 is the Western calendar year 1932. The Kawasaki Type 92 fighter was completed in 1932 in the Western calendar, and the Type 88 was completed in 1928.) The aircraft industry is mostly due to its own unique initiative. Although it has not reached the level of all-metal manufacturing, the Kawasaki Shipbuilding Aircraft Factory has manufactured three types according to the Tronier formula. Recently, Mitsubishi Aircraft Co., Ltd. built the Yuan Jia Si G38 (a giant aircraft equipped with four engines). Kawanishi Aviation Co., Ltd. built a giant all-metal seaplane. The Guang Naval Factory surpasses individual factories and strives for improvement. Its excellent skills are like the giant all-metal seaplane Type 90-1, made in 1930, equipped with three Ise-Bano 700-horsepower engines.

A Glimpse of the Aircraft Factory

Japan currently has six major civilian aircraft factories, namely Mitsubishi, Kawasaki, Kawanishi, Ishikawajima, Nakajima, and Aichi Clock Electric. There are also five aircraft engine manufacturers, such as Mitsubishi, Kawasaki, Nakajima, Aichi, and Tokyo Gas Electric. These factories are dedicated to the production of military aircraft and do not manufacture export products. However, recently, Nakajima Manufacturing Co. manufactured five Fokker-style passenger aircraft and sold them to the newly established Manchurian Air Transport Company. In terms of the manufacture of military aircraft, the Army also has Nagoya and Chikusak factories. The Navy has the Hiroshima and Yokosuka naval factories. Generally, military designs are often used, but for the benefit of civilian companies, civilian designs are sometimes also used. Government supervision is very strict. New types of aircraft are not allowed to be made public. Today, Japan can also imitate high-horsepower engines designed by Japan, such as Ise-Bano, Napier, Lorraine, Kubei, and BMW.

Inspection and Design Competition

For new aircraft manufactured by civilian companies according to government designs, the Navy has strict inspections at the Yokosuka Naval Factory, and the Army has strict inspections at the Tachikawa Aviation Technical Headquarters (the reporter was introduced by Principal Kinoshita in the 9th year of the Republic of China and visited the three factories. Except for the aircraft manufacturing parts that are allowed to be visited, the rest are strictly secret.) In order to promote the development of the civilian aircraft industry, the government has held flight competitions to allow aircraft manufactured by civilian companies to participate. If an aircraft is considered to be superior, it will be adopted as a military aircraft. The Nakajima Type 91 fighter (air-cooled) and the Kawasaki Type 92 fighter (water-cooled) are examples of this. The relationship between the government and the aircraft manufacturing industry is extremely close. In terms of civilian aspects, if foreign models are needed, Mitsubishi Mitsui often purchases them from foreign countries. During this period, the promotion of famous newspapers in various ports has been particularly powerful in promoting the development of the Japanese aviation industry. Although, the Japanese aviation industry has made great leaps in recent years, its current efforts are far inferior to those of the major countries in the world. However, recently, it has been realized the importance of air defense, and the people have all realized the power of aviation to protect the country. At the same time, the manufacture of warships and submarines has also received great assistance from the people.

Naval Aircraft Manufacturing

Since 1909, Japan has understood the effectiveness of aircraft in ocean warfare. The naval committee of 21 people, including Colonel K. Yamamuro, researched the performance. The following year, five officers were dispatched to the United States and France to study aircraft technology. At the same time, three mechanical lieutenants were sent to Europe and the United States to study institutions. One of the three is now the director of the Nakajima Aircraft Manufacturing Plant, named Mr. Nakajima Chikuhei. In 1912, Prince Kaya brought back two Florman seaplanes from France and two Curtis seaplanes from the United States. After returning to China, he immediately set up an aircraft field near Yokosuka Naval Port and trained six young aviators. At the end of 1913, the Navy had 100-horsepower and 140-horsepower Gnome engines. Afterwards, it purchased two more Deperdussin seaplanes with greater speed from France. The pilots who operated this new aircraft were the naval aviators who were trained. During this period, naval technicians personally manufactured seaplanes. After several trials, the Florman airship was manufactured using domestic materials. At the same time, the number of aviators also increased year by year. Later, the Navy remodeled the transport ship Wakamiya into the first aircraft carrier, equipped with five Florman aircraft for trial maritime flights. In 1914, Wakamiya transported seaplanes to Qingdao to begin reconnaissance and bombing of fortresses. In 1915, the engine also had the Japanese-made Florman type, which could fly in the air for ten hours. This was the performance of the engine manufactured at the naval factory at the end of 1914. The test results were also excellent. At the end of World War I, De Lia military boats were purchased from France. The following year, a De Lia airship equipped with two Ise-Bano Sisha 300-horsepower engines was purchased. Since then, efforts have been made to research large airships. In 1919, 60% of military aircraft were made of Japanese materials. In 1918, the Navy, due to the expansion of the Naval Air Force, established a large aircraft manufacturing plant in Wu Naval Port. When the plant was completed, it was said to have the capacity to manufacture 60 aircraft per month. Before long, a naval aircraft manufacturing plant appeared in Tokyo.

Training of Naval Aviators

In 1912, construction began on the aircraft carrier Hosho Maru. At the same time, it was deeply felt that naval flight required land-based control. A large naval aircraft field was established in Kasumigaura. In the same year, Lieutenant Colonel Shembial and others of the British Air Force were recruited to serve as naval instructors, and seaplanes, land-based aircraft, flying boats and engines were purchased from the United Kingdom. On the one hand, private companies established Mitsubishi, Kawasaki, Aichi, Nakajima, and other companies to manufacture military aircraft. After the war, Mitsubishi manufactured naval training aircraft. In 1922, the first aircraft carrier Hosho Maru was completed, and aircraft became part of the fleet. By 1923, all-metal large airships began to research and test Rohrback and Tronier airships. By 1930, the all-metal monoplane airship Type 90-1 (equipped with three Ise-Bano 700-horsepower engines) was completed at the Guang Naval Factory. In the same year, a Shuttleworth airship (equipped with three Rolls-Royce 800-horsepower engines) was purchased from the United Kingdom. Kawanishi Aircraft Manufacturing Plant obtained the construction rights of the Shuttleworth formula and began manufacturing. The Guang Factory's Type 90-1 is considered the standard naval aircraft. In 1925, the Navy's Type 4, equipped with a Lorraine 400-horsepower engine, was designated as a seaplane reconnaissance aircraft. The following year, the performance of the Lorraine 450-horsepower engine was improved. All three multi-seat aircraft were loaded on Japanese battleships and cruisers. The Navy's standard two-seat reconnaissance aircraft was the Ise-Bano 300-horsepower Type 15, which was a remodeled British Hansa-Brandenburg aircraft. Equipped with two Lorraine 450-horsepower engines, its organization was repeatedly improved. After the aircraft was completed, it was first tested several times between Yokosuka and the Marshall Islands (approximately 2,500 nautical miles). In 1928, the Gloster Gambet (Curtis 450-horsepower) won the competition for the best carrier-based fighter, and manufacturing rights were purchased from the United Kingdom. This aircraft was the first aerial battle in the Orient. During the Shanghai Incident, it competed with Chinese fighter aircraft (piloted by the American Schuttleworth) and finally shot down the aircraft. In 1929, the Navy's Type 89 biplane bomber was completed. Its same capacity has not yet been made public. It is feared that it is equipped with Ise-Bano or Rolls-Royce, a 650-horsepower excellent bomber with an 18-inch torpedo and a cruising range of 750 nautical miles. In 1930, the Nakajima-made Type 90 fighter, the Kawanishi-made Type 90 reconnaissance aircraft, and the Navy's Type 90-1 seaplane reconnaissance aircraft (all equipped with Curtis 450-horsepower engines) were adopted by the Navy. The current Hognem-Lord carrier-based single-seat fighter is also being tested by the naval factory. The manufacturing machine was first purchased from the United Kingdom. Today, Japan is striving to imitate several types of carrier-based bombers, carrier-based two-seat fighters, large flying boats for coastal patrol, etc. The Navy authorities are very strict in inspection.

Impressions of the New British Envoy to China

Sir Knatchbull-Hugessen Served in Geneva for a Long Time

Also Very Familiar with Our Country's Envoys Yen and Shih

Reuter's report from London on the 3rd states, it has been an open secret in political circles here for several weeks that Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen is to succeed as British Envoy to China, which has now been officially verified today. This reporter specially drove to Sir Hugessen's London residence to interview him for a long time. Although Sir Hugessen has not yet been to China, he has been serving in the British delegation office in Geneva for a long time, and he has interacted with people from various countries, and he is also very familiar with China's Ambassador to Russia, Yen Hui-ching, and Minister to the United States, Shih Chao-chi. According to the personal impressions of this reporter, it seems that Sir Hugessen is very familiar with the various special issues that should be handled during his tenure as the Envoy to China. Sir Hugessen must now take a trip abroad, and then stay in the Foreign Office for some time. It is expected that he will not be able to start his journey to China before January next year.

Guangzhou's Invisible Martial Law

An Extreme Manifestation of Terror

Military and Political Figures Repeatedly Arrested

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, a blue terror scene has been extremely manifested here. The authorities have long been secretly investigating and arresting, successively cracking down on organizations and executing a reporter surnamed Hou from a Hong Kong newspaper by shooting (a student of Zhongshan University). Also, a member of the executive committee of a certain county's party department was arrested and imprisoned. There have also been several cases of active and retired military and political figures being detained. In mid-September, an invisible martial law was imposed on the entire city of Guangzhou. This was because the authorities found communications from so-called Blue Shirt Party members in the mail, and investigated and arrested people according to the addresses. Yesterday, several suspects were taken to the Public Security Bureau from a certain place. Those who were working in institutions included two employees of the Works Department of the Yuehan Railway, one employee of the Cleaning Section of a certain bureau, and two people from a certain senior military institution, all of whom have been detained. On the evening of the 19th, the authorities again dispatched armed police to No. 4 Lian Residence, Tongfu West Back Street, Henan Island, and, together with the police, arrested several well-dressed men from the residence and took them to the Public Security Bureau for secret interrogation. It was found that the Lian Residence was the residence of Lian Bingzhang, the former commander of the 16th Division of the Fifth Army (Li Fulin's troops). Lian Bingzhang was also arrested and questioned that night. On the 20th, the headquarters of the First Army Group also suspected He Yilu, the current captain of the Jiangda warship, of being a member of the Blue Shirt Party. At about 1 p.m. that afternoon, Chen Jitang used the telephone to order Zhang Zhiying, the commander of the fleet, to have He come to the headquarters, saying that he had something to discuss in person. Zhang then informed He and went to the headquarters, where Chen personally met him, asked a question or two, and then telegraphed Zhang Zhiying to come to the headquarters and take He back to the fleet headquarters for custody. He also sent two adjutants to search He's residence in Taiping Sha. All documents and correspondence were taken back to the headquarters for review. At about 4 p.m. on the 21st, investigators at the headquarters learned that a certain residence outside the police boundary in the northern suburbs, which was not listed with a house number, was a general meeting place for a certain reactionary organization. Chen Jitang immediately ordered the headquarters of the military police to send out detectives and military police to search. However, the people involved had already fled after hearing the news. Only a large number of important documents and leaflets were found in the organization. Therefore, all military and political institutions in Guangzhou suddenly imposed martial law that night. The headquarters of the First Army Group added military police to stand guard and patrol from evening to 6 a.m. the next morning, from Zhengnan Road in the east to Hua Ningli in the south, to the side of Central Park in the west, and to Dexuan East Road in the north. From 11 p.m., passers-by could not pass without a password. The defense was withdrawn at 6 a.m. on the 22nd. The Public Security Bureau also implemented martial law on the same night, and armed police were sent to guard all areas near Weixin Road. Although the curfew was short, it was enough to see the situation in Guangzhou. (September 25th)

Page 13

Guangdong Province to Levy Tax on Imported Agricultural Products

Special Tax Bureau Limits Rice Merchants to Declare and Pay Taxes

Investigation of Tax Rates on Miscellaneous Imported Agricultural Products

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangdong Provincial Government has decided to levy a foreign rice tax of one yuan per hundred catties and also a foreign grain tax of six jiao per hundred catties. Rice merchants in Guangzhou have not yet complied with the implementation. However, the Special Tax Bureau for Imported Agricultural Products has already opened on the 16th. Branch bureaus have also been established in the Five Counties, Qiongyai, and Chao Mei areas, and personnel have been dispatched to start collecting taxes. Branch checkpoints have been set up in Ershui, Shenzhen, and Chencun to prevent smuggling. The Guangzhou Agricultural Tax Bureau has already sent a letter to the Guangzhou Rice Merchants Association, urging them to pay the tax arrears and sending personnel to various rice shops to persuade them, limiting them to pay in accordance with the regulations within three days. The tax rates for the collection of miscellaneous special taxes on imported agricultural products are as follows: Caviar, milk shortcake, honey, fruit jam, fruit juice, frozen soy sauce, sarsaparilla, and other unnamed seasonings, all are taxed at 15 yuan per hundred yuan of cargo value. Chocolate, cocoa, coffee, the above three items are taxed at 12 yuan per hundred yuan of cargo value. Lard, apples (in addition to the public fees payable by the provincial Chen Xian Guo Xian Huo industry) are taxed at 7 yuan, 5 jiao and 5 fen. Unnamed dried fruits, fresh fruits, oranges (including Jinsheng orange, lemon, etc.) in addition to the public fees payable by the provincial Chen Xian Guo Xian Huo industry are taxed at 7 yuan, 5 jiao and 5 fen. Salted pork, foreign ham (such as canned and other loaded tax 3 yuan) fish, seafood, canned food, and various meats are taxed at 10 yuan per hundred yuan of cargo value. Baking powder, corned beef, biscuits, the above three items are taxed at 8 yuan per hundred yuan of cargo value. Mushrooms (this item is taxed by the catty) are taxed at 7 yuan per hundred yuan. Asparagus fruit and biscuit ingredients, gravy, condensed milk, olive oil, artificial cream (wheat flour is exempt) almond rice, in addition to paying the Beijing fruit and seafood donation, is taxed at 3 yuan and 5 jiao. Mountain chestnuts are taxed at 5 yuan per hundred yuan of cargo value. Small raisins, wild bird eggs, poultry eggs, light cream, light milk, milk powder, dried meat, pork skin, the above items are taxed at 3 yuan per hundred yuan of cargo value. White bird's nest (taxed by the catty) is taxed at 2 yuan and 5 jiao per catty. Fennel, star anise, are taxed at 2 yuan per hundred yuan of cargo value. Galangal is taxed at 1 yuan and 5 jiao per hundred catties. All miscellaneous imported agricultural products transported into the mainland must be valued and taxed. The valuation method is based on the customs valuation standard. Goods vendors who report more or less, or report high or low, or imply leakage for taxable goods, will be charged three times the tax amount. Those who refuse inspection, pursuit, or resist arrest will be reported to the Department of Finance for investigation and confiscation. (September 26th)

Recent Developments in the Suppression of Bandits in the Border Areas of Sichuan, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, and Anhui

Liu Zhenhua to Concurrently Supervise Post-War Rehabilitation

He Chengjun Goes to Sichuan on Jiang's Orders

Hankou Correspondence: Chairman Jiang has specially appointed Tian Songyao as the Bandit Suppression Supervisor of Sichuan Province, to supervise the suppression of Xu Xiangqian's remnants, Xu Yuanquan as the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the Hunan-Hubei Border Region, to supervise the suppression of He Long's remnants, and Liu Zhenhua as the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the Henan-Hubei-Anhui Border Region, to supervise the suppression of Kuang Jixun's remnants, while entrusting He Chengjun, the Pacification Director stationed in Hubei, to be in charge of the overall situation. Later, due to the situation in Sichuan, Tian Songyao's troops suffered repeated defeats, and Liu Xiang was appointed as the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in Sichuan Province, taking full responsibility. In the past two months, Liu Zhenhua has supervised Liu Maoen, Sun Lianzhong, Liang Guanying, Song Tiancai, Hao Mengling, Shangguan Yunxiang, Peng Zhenshan, Wan Yaohuang, and Dai Minquan to advance and suppress bandits in multiple routes, repeatedly attacking bandit dens. There are no longer any traces of bandits in the border area between Henan and Anhui. Although the area around Huang'an and Macheng in eastern Hubei has not yet been completely cleared, the main force has indeed been broken. In addition to continuing the suppression, Liu is also working on post-war rehabilitation. When He Chengjun went to Lushan to meet Jiang, he entrusted Li Shucheng, a member of the Hubei Provincial Committee, to go with him, requesting Chairman Jiang to designate the counties in the Henan-Hubei-Anhui border region as special administrative regions and to raise 4.9 million yuan for post-war rehabilitation. Liu's reasons for the proposal are: (1) The areas in the border region of the three provinces that have been ravaged by bandits have been for as long as seven years and as short as two or three years. The rural areas have been completely destroyed, and the people have been deeply redized. Without special politics, the root cause cannot be rectified and the bandit disaster will never be eliminated. Therefore, it is necessary to establish special administrative regions. (2) Rural areas in the border region are bankrupt, and the disaster situation is extremely serious. After the recovery, the resettlement of refugees, encouraging them to cultivate, as well as emergency relief, work relief, and agricultural relief all require funds. A post-war rehabilitation fund of 4.9 million yuan is not enough to inject funds. When He and Li met Jiang and asked for instructions in person, Jiang indicated that he would adopt the proposal and set up a post-war rehabilitation supervisor in the special administrative regions divided in the three provinces to preside over the matter. It is also heard that Liu Zhenhua will be appointed to this position concurrently, so that orders can be unified and military and political affairs can be planned together. This measure will probably be realized in a few days. He bandits in the Hunan-Hubei border region have been heavily damaged by Xu Yuanquan's supervision and the joint efforts of the Hunan and Hubei troops. Not long ago, although they once captured Songzi and fled south on a large scale, they soon retreated into Hunan. Xu Yuanquan and Fan Xiji have gone to Yichang from Shashi via the mountains in the Hunan-Hubei border region to go to Shihe to supervise the suppression. The future is optimistic. Xu bandits in Sichuan Province occupy Tongnanba and other counties in northern Sichuan and have not yet been recovered. Although the Sichuan provincial troops have claimed to advance and suppress, they have not yet sent troops. Only Liu Cunhou, Tian Songyao, and their old and weak remnants are dealing with them. Now Liu Xiang has set October 1st to take office as the Commander-in-Chief in Chengdu, and has asked Jiang to specially send senior officials to Sichuan to supervise the oath and give instructions. Jiang has appointed He Chengjun as the supervising committee member. He will take a plane from Ganzhou to Hankou on the 24th, and is scheduled to fly to Chongqing from Hankou on the 27th with Qiu Jia, Liu Xiang's representative, and Zeng Kuangqing, a member of the Central Committee, and then go to Chengdu. After Liu Xiang takes office, he will convene a bandit suppression military conference of Sichuan generals Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, Liu Cunhou, Yang Sen, and second-tier generals Wang Lingji, etc. to determine the overall plan and mobilize on a large scale. On the way back, he will go to Shihe in western Hubei to inspect the bandit suppression situation of Xu's troops and hold a meeting with Xu Yuanquan and other generals to discuss ways to completely eliminate the He bandits. After returning to Hankou, he will go to southern and northern Hubei to continue his inspection. (September 25th)

Wujiang, Upstream of Nanjing, Captured by Bandits

- Nearby Towns Mostly Looted -

Wuhu Correspondence: He County, across the river from Caishi upstream of Nanjing, Kunlian, Quanjiao, and Jiangpu County in Jiangsu Province produce a lot of cotton, and business is prosperous. Recently, a large number of bandits suddenly appeared, looting nearby towns. Last night, the Jingwu merchant ship from Jing arrived in Wuhu, carrying many refugees. According to them, Wujiang Town, He County, was besieged by four or five hundred bandits the day before (27th). Most of the bandits were wearing white plain clothes and claimed to be part of the Zhang Dabizi bandit group who had previously captured Hanshan County. Although the soldiers of the anti-smuggling battalion and the security team stationed there gathered to resist, they were defeated due to being outnumbered. The bandits drove straight in, first confiscating the firearms of the Public Security Bureau and the Special Tax Office, and then wantonly looting. Wealthy families were led by local ruffians to plunder. They are still entrenched in the town and forbid all the people in the town to go out. The bandits came from upstream of Wujiang. Chizhen, the first town of Quanjiao County, and Xiangquan Street, He County, were also ransacked and all the firearms and weapons of the security team were confiscated. The details of the losses cannot be detailed because the merchant ship did not dare to stop after passing Wujiang. After the bandits occupied Wujiang, a part of them advanced along the river through Shibahe towards He County. On the one hand, he sent an urgent telegram to the commissioners' offices of the second and fifth districts for help. One hundred and twenty security team members were transferred here last night and rushed to help defend by the Depu special ship overnight. The Salt Affairs Inspection Office also received a report of heavy losses. (September 29th)

(September 27th)

Labor-Management Dispute at Yufeng Yarn Factory in Henan

- A Person Familiar with the Situation at Yufeng Yarn Factory Talks -

According to someone familiar with the situation at the Yufeng Yarn Factory in Zhengzhou, the factory stopped work on July 29 this year due to business losses and a lack of cotton. At that time, the factory announced the termination of the workers' contracts in accordance with Article 30 of the Factory Law, and paid the wages for the notice period in accordance with the same law. This would have allowed them to end all past processes and reorganize freely when work resumed in the future, so as to obtain a new life. Unexpectedly, the official authorities intervened based on the request of the trade union and advocated paying the workers' maintenance fees during the shutdown period. Although the mediation method stipulated that the factory had the right to increase or decrease and freely hire workers, the factory was recently opposed by the trade union when it was preparing to resume work and reorganize, which led to new disputes. Recent news about the labor-management dispute at the factory, as reported in various newspapers, is mostly one-sided and does not fully correspond to the facts. Therefore, the truth is restated as follows:

The Yufeng Yarn Factory was established in Zhengzhou, Henan Province, for the purpose of developing the inland industry. Since 1927, due to its location and trends, it has been controlled by the trade union. In the past six or seven years, there have been no less than 20 various demands, often with the threat of guns. A former associate manager of the factory was robbed by armed workers and almost met with an accident. Because of the irresistible force, the factory's monthly expenditure on wages alone increased from 30,000 yuan to more than 50,000 yuan, increasing the annual expenditure by about 300,000 yuan. The working hours were reduced from 12 hours per shift to 10 hours, and work was stopped for 4 hours per day, resulting in uncompensated losses. However, the number of workers could not be reduced, resulting in huge costs. Over the years, the business has been losing money and it has been almost impossible to maintain. The factory, seeing that the factory affairs were so difficult and could not last, tried its best to study and improve the machines. In the autumn of 1930, it invented the Mujuzhi large extension and immediately improved all the machines to increase production and reduce losses. Unexpectedly, the trade union took this as its own achievement and demanded a huge bonus. Although there were still losses in the year-end accounts, the factory still paid a bonus of 43,000 yuan due to pressure from the official authorities. The following year, they made another request. After several months of stalemate, the result was that the factory still paid a bonus of 60,000 yuan due to the mediation of the official authorities. This year, the factory suffered even greater losses due to cotton yarn and had to stop work. It was originally intended to pay severance in accordance with the Factory Law in order to thoroughly reorganize, but this was not achieved because the official authorities listened only to the one-sided words of the trade union and advocated paying maintenance fees. However, the factory is a commercial enterprise and will continue to lose money. This time, the factory will follow the general practice of yarn factories across the country, setting the working hours at 12 hours per shift (if the government can uniformly change all factories across the country to 10 hours per shift, the factory will also be very willing to comply), and reducing the number of workers per 10,000 spindles to more than 540, which is still a huge difference compared to the 240 workers employed by Japanese-owned yarn factories in China. This is the minimum reform. If it cannot be done, the factory will not be able to maintain. In recent years, there has been a lot of silver in Shanghai, so people dare not invest in developing industries in the interior, because they cannot get political protection when running industries in the interior. If the government really wants to increase production, it must start by protecting inland industries. The factory has suffered great sacrifices due to the times. I wonder whether the government, which has a policy of increasing production, can open a way for inland industries. The solution to the factory's dispute will be known.

Jiangyin

Ignorance of Bombs Almost Causes Great Disaster

Zhang Falin, a carpenter from Changzhou and Yangliupu, West Wai Xingchun Street, has a wife, sons, and six family members. Yesterday (29th), his eldest son Jiwen, 16, picked up a grenade the size of an egg by the river. Not knowing what it was, he threw the bomb into the stove to burn while he was cooking lunch. Unexpectedly, there was a loud explosion, the earthen stove was shattered, and the vegetables in the pot went straight to the roof. Falin's wife had one ear blown off, and her legs and hands were all seriously injured. Jiwen's hair and face were also blown off. The injured were taken to the Gospel Hospital for treatment and are not in life-threatening condition.

Because her son, Jiarui, was helping out at a clothing shop outside Ximen in Nantong, she went to search for him but did not find him. She was already short of travel money, so she went to Xicheng from Jiangyin, which led to her drowning. It is also tragic.

Verdict in Chief's Rape Case Announced

The case of Guo Chenjiu, the former chief of the West Lake Special Tax Bureau, raping Zhou Zhuoying, the daughter of the late Zhou Guifang, a clerk of the bureau, has been in court since it was reported. Guo died of madness. The Hangzhou Local Court found that the second defendant in the case, Guo Guozhen (Guo Zi) and Jing Guoshi, were both guilty of helping to rape a girl under the age of 20, and sentenced each of them to one year and two months of imprisonment. Guo Guozhen was fined 1,000 yuan and Jing Guoshi was fined 300 yuan. Zhou Zhuoying requested 20,000 yuan in civil damages and the immigration court handled the case. Guo and others were not satisfied and appealed to the High Court. After the trial, the verdict was announced at 2 p.m. yesterday (30th). The original verdict was overturned. Guo Guozhen and Jing Guoshi were both found not guilty. Zhou Zhuoying's incidental civil suit was dismissed. It is heard that Zhou Zhuoying and her mother plan to appeal again.

Bandit Attempts Kidnapping and is Apprehended

Ding Youquan, a bandit from Shashaikeng, the border between Xinchang and Shengxian, has repeatedly committed kidnapping and extortion. He was captured by the Xinchang County Government last November. After being released on bail after being a mole to kill the bandit leader Bingxian, Ding fled to Shanghai and hid in the home of Hu Dasan at No. 7 Liushuiqiao, Songmuchi. One day, he met Liang Xiaocai, a fellow villager, and learned that Liang was living in the home of his aunt's husband, Yang Jintang, who was very wealthy and lived at No. 57 Shihuqiao, Xidajie. Yang himself was a battalion commander in the Nanchang Headquarters. Ding suddenly had a bad idea and discussed with Liang to kidnap Yang's three-year-old son, Shiyuan, in order to extort a large sum of money. Ding gave Liang 500 yuan as a reward and ordered him to take the child out, because Liang had previously cooperated with Ding in robberies. Later, Liang returned home, had a change of heart, and reported it to his aunt, who reported it to the police station in charge. Yesterday (30th), the two criminals, Ding and Liang, were arrested and interrogated.

Due to the Old Jiang Bridge not being repaired yet, the fire engines from both sides of the Jiang River within the city were unable to reach the scene for rescue. Only the An'an Fire Brigade's fire engine arrived to provide assistance. It took half an hour to extinguish the fire. A total of seven shops, including Lin Shengfa's firewood shop, were affected, with over ten houses burned down, resulting in losses exceeding ten thousand taels of silver.

Damage from the Typhoon in Zhenhai County

The coastal towns and villages of Zhenhai County suffered extremely heavy damage from the recent typhoon. After the county magistrate, Xu Yong, personally inspected the affected areas, it was found that about 20% of the county's households, approximately over 30,000 households, were affected. Eight people, including men, women, and children, drowned. Over 300 tiled houses were completely destroyed, and over 1,000 were partially destroyed. Over 1,000 thatched houses were completely destroyed, along with over 100 boats. Thousands of salt pan planks were washed away, and 200,000 to 300,000 catties of salt were lost. Breaches occurred along approximately 200 li of coastal dikes, and over 100,000 mu of cotton fields were flooded. The harvest of crops in the fields was greatly reduced due to the intrusion of saltwater. The total losses are estimated to be over 3 million taels of silver, making it an unprecedented disaster in decades. The county magistrate left for Shanghai yesterday, and Shanghai-based gentry and merchants are raising relief funds to help the disaster-stricken people. Furthermore, in the vicinity of Daishan, Nianmu, Tiebansha, and other places, about 50 to 60 floating corpses have been retrieved in recent days, including both men and women, mostly fishermen from Chongming. The scene is extremely tragic.

Those who are willing to take on this position are requested to send three correspondence samples first, clearly stating their address and occupation. If this newspaper deems them qualified, the terms and conditions will be communicated immediately. Those who are not qualified will not receive a reply. This notice is hereby given.

Wang, Sun, Song, Kong, Li, and Others Visited Song Yesterday Morning to Confer on Finance

Wang Indicates That He Has Discussed Considerable Relief Measures

Sun, Li, Gu, and Tang Arrive in Shanghai Together

Railway Minister Gu Mengyu and Vice Foreign Minister Tang Youren arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning by express train, arriving at the port at approximately 2:00 p.m.

Financial Issues Discussed at Song's Residence

At 9:00 a.m. yesterday, Executive Yuan President Wang Jingwei first went to Song's residence to meet with Finance Minister Song Ziwen. Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke followed at 9:25 a.m. At 9:20 a.m., Central Bank Governor Kong Xiangxi went to Wang's residence on Pushi Road to visit Wang, but Wang had already gone to Song's residence, so Kong drove there to join the meeting. At 11:20 a.m., Central Committee Member Li Shizeng also arrived. Wang, Sun, Song, Kong, Li, and others immediately held a meeting in the living room of Song's residence to conduct a comprehensive discussion on various important issues, including central finances, the reorganization and progress of the National Economic Commission, and the disposition of American cotton and wheat. Wang, Sun, and others left successively at 11:40 a.m. It is heard that after this long discussion, opinions from all parties were unified, and considerable relief measures were also discussed for central finances.

Jiang Talks About Having Financial Solutions

After leaving Song's residence at 11:40 a.m., Wang drove to the Wanglu residence on Haige Road to visit Mayor Wu Tiecheng, but he was not there, so he left. He then quickly returned to his private residence at 11:50 a.m. and immediately met with a group of reporters, making the following statement: He said that his visit to Shanghai this time was to discuss central financial issues with Minister Song, because the central military and administrative expenses had indeed reached a point of exhaustion. Today (i.e., yesterday) was also the end of the month, and this month's expenses urgently needed to be paid. Therefore, immediately after the Central Political Council meeting, he came to Shanghai to discuss solutions with Minister Song. In addition, they discussed the organization and progress of the National Economic Commission. Those who met at Song's residence this morning (i.e., yesterday morning) included Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke, Finance Minister Song Ziwen, Central Bank Governor Kong Xiangxi, Central Committee Member Li Shizeng, and himself. As a result of the discussions, relief measures were discussed for central finances. He was unable to disclose the detailed contents.

Cotton and Wheat Loans to Be Used for Construction

Wang also stated that regarding the use of American cotton and wheat loans, it had been declared earlier that they would be used for construction and production projects. Although military and administrative expenses are extremely difficult, they must not be easily diverted. This principle was unanimously advocated during this morning's discussion and must not be changed. As for the finances of North China, Minister Song and Chairman Huang have agreed that they will be directly under the central government's jurisdiction in the future.

Active Responsibility, Resignation Is Inaccurate

When reporters asked about the rumors that Minister Song had submitted his resignation and that Chairman Chiang and President Wang himself also had the intention of resigning, inquiring as to the truth, Wang responded that this statement could be proven by the facts. Minister Song advocated using American cotton and wheat loans for construction and production projects, and other committee members also had the same aspirations, without any differences of opinion. Since the views of the various committee members are the same, the rumor that Song became passive due to disagreement is self-defeating. In this time of national crisis, we can only actively take responsibility and strive to save the country and ensure its survival. Wang also said that if anyone can take responsibility for them, they can abdicate at any time, so there is no question of resignation or non-resignation.

Economic Commission to Be Established Next Week

The National Economic Commission is scheduled to be established in Nanjing next Wednesday or Thursday. Minister Song is in Shanghai, planning financial matters, and will return to Nanjing in about two or three days to formally take office as a standing committee member of the Economic Commission. As for the Economic Commission, it will be based entirely on assigning personnel to tasks and will not set up institutions first and then assign personnel. For example, cotton industry relief is currently important, so a Cotton Industry Control Committee has been specially established. The rumor of expanding the organization is completely inaccurate. The position of Secretary-General will be held by Qin Fen, director of the preparatory office of the commission. All matters have been handled by him in the past, so he will continue to be hired to leverage his expertise. As for the Construction Committee, it will not be merged for the time being, etc.

Wang Visits Huang Fu; Huang to Go North Tonight

At 3:00 p.m. yesterday, Wang drove to Qiqi Road to visit Huang Fu, chairman of the Peace Preservation and Administration Committee, for about two hours. When Wang left, he told a reporter from the Xin Xin News Agency that his visit to Huang was to conduct a final consultation on issues such as the finances of North China. After thorough discussions with Huang, they have now been completely agreed upon. Huang has decided to take the Shanghai-Beijing through train back to Beijing from Shanghai at 11:00 p.m. tomorrow night (i.e., tonight) and will not linger in Nanjing, etc. Yesterday afternoon, when President Wang was at Huang's residence, Vice Foreign Minister Tang Youren and Railway Minister Gu Mengyu also visited Huang one after another and left after Wang.

Mayor Hosts Banquet; Returns to Beijing Today

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng hosted a banquet for Executive Yuan President Wang Jingwei at the Municipal Government Reception Center on Xiafei Road at 12:00 noon yesterday. Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke, Finance Minister Song Ziwen, Central Bank Governor Kong Xiangxi, Envoy to Japan Jiang Zuobin, Peace Preservation and Administration Committee Chairman Huang Fu, Central Committee Member Li Shizeng, and others were invited to attend. The guests and hosts dispersed in high spirits at about 2:00 p.m. Wang Jingwei is scheduled to return to Nanjing today, and Sun Ke will stay in Shanghai for a while and return to Nanjing in two or three days, it is said.

Minister to Mexico Huang Yingsu Arrives in Shanghai

Will Depart Overseas to Assume His New Post as Soon as Arrangements Are Completed

There were originally over 40,000 overseas Chinese in Mexico, most of whom were engaged in agriculture and commerce, and who have made many contributions to Mexico. Therefore, they are highly valued by the Mexican government. Recently, the people of the Shanshan and Suen provinces of Mexico have been affected by the global economic recession, and their businesses have declined. Seeing that the overseas Chinese are engaged in business in these areas, not only are there many of them, but they are also hardworking and able to endure hardship. Therefore, they have been looked upon with resentment by some Mexicans. Some Mexicans believe that their commerce has been encroached upon by the overseas Chinese. Thus, regardless of diplomatic relations, they have organized an anti-Chinese party to implement discrimination, confiscate property, and expel them. It is difficult for the overseas Chinese to gain a foothold, so many have returned to their home country from places such as San Francisco and Los Angeles, accounting for nearly half of them. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is very concerned about this matter and has collected a large number of documents for reference in negotiations. On the one hand, the government has newly appointed Huang Yingsu as the minister to Mexico to take charge. Huang went to Nanjing from Shanghai the day before yesterday to pay his respects to Wang Jingwei, who is both the Executive Yuan President and Foreign Minister, to ask for instructions on the policies to be adopted after going to Mexico and to prepare the credentials and handle passport procedures. All matters have been completed. He returned to Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday. It is heard that Huang is taking care of personal matters in Shanghai. As soon as the arrangements are completed, he plans to depart overseas to assume his new post in Mexico in the coming days.

Dismantling of Cross-Border Telephones Began Yesterday

Pudong Postponed for Now

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, in accordance with the provisional contract signed with the Shanghai Telephone Company, began dismantling cross-border telephones yesterday and is actively preparing to establish the Pudong Branch. However, the cross-border telephones in Pudong will be dismantled only after the branch is established. The details are as follows:

Dismantling Begins: The Shanghai Telephone Company installed a total of 288 cross-border telephones in Zhabei, Nanshi, Pudong, Longhua, Huxi, and other places. After the Shanghai Telephone Bureau announced the dismantling of cross-border telephones, at 9:00 a.m. yesterday, the engineering department dispatched mechanics to Nanshi and Zhabei to dismantle the telephone lines of businesses that had first requested the removal of cross-border telephones. There were seven in Nanshi and six in Zhabei. As for the remaining cross-border telephones in Nanshi, Zhabei, Longhua, Huxi, and other places, mechanics will be dispatched again starting today to continue dismantling them. However, the cross-border telephones of the Municipal Government and its affiliated bureaus, as well as the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Garrison Headquarters, will be dismantled only after all the cross-border telephones of businesses and factories have been completely dismantled.

Pudong Postponed: There are a total of 77 cross-border telephones in Pudong. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau is actively proceeding with the preparation and installation of the Pudong Telephone Branch. The telephone lines of the bureau will be implemented after the branch is established. Therefore, in order to facilitate telephone communication between businesses, factories, and wharves in Pudong, the cross-border telephones in Pudong will be temporarily suspended from dismantling. The Pudong Branch is scheduled to be established in early November. Fifty pairs of lines leading to Pudong will be added at Gaochang Temple to prepare for the installation of telephones in Pudong.

First Batch of American Cotton Began to Be Unloaded Yesterday

11,350 Pieces

All Unloaded into China Merchants' Wharf

The first batch of American cotton purchased by China through American loans, which arrived on the American vessel "Aisanya Alan," has been unloaded at the China Merchants' Wharf in Pudong. Yesterday, workers were dispatched from the dock to lift the cotton from the ship using cranes and store it in the warehouses. The number of pieces of cotton unloaded into the warehouse was 11,350, as stated on the ship's manifest, and all were unloaded and stacked in various warehouses in China Merchants' Wharf without being stored elsewhere. The previous report that only 4,500 pieces remained in the China Merchants' Wharf was a misreport. The actual number of pieces in the warehouse is indeed 11,350 bales, as previously reported by this newspaper. After being stacked in the warehouse, the future unloading issue, as learned by reporters, will be handled by buyers at any time, at their convenience, without any restrictions on the storage period. Furthermore, the Ministry of Finance is fully responsible for the goods upon arrival at the warehouse. Once sold, the government will no longer be responsible for any issues until the goods are unloaded from the warehouse.

Members of the Provisional Municipal Council Resign En Masse

Discussing the Municipal Budget and Disaster Area Reconstruction Plan

The Shanghai Municipal Council held its Fourth Meeting of the Second Regular Session the day before yesterday. Councilors Shi Liangcai, Chen Bingqian, Guo Shun, Qin Runqing, Xu Yongzuo, Du Yuesheng, Tao Baichuan, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Yansong, Wang Xiaolai, and others were present, constituting a quorum. Chairman Shi Liangcai announced the opening of the meeting and gave a report, followed by the discussion of agenda items. The following are some of the important cases:

Municipal Budget

Regarding the municipal revenue and expenditure budget for this year (1933), after being reviewed by the Municipal Government, the Council considered the budget to be of great importance and specially formed a budget review committee. However, since there were no financial statements from the previous year for comparison, it was difficult to review whether the created budget was suitable for the actual revenue and expenditure situation. Therefore, it sent a letter to the Municipal Government, requesting that the financial statements be sent to the Council as soon as possible. In response, the Municipal Government sent a letter stating that although the budget for 1931 had been approved by the Central Government, there had been changes due to war. The budget for 1932 had only recently been approved. Therefore, a considerable amount of time was required to compile the financial statements for each year. As a result of the budget review committee meeting, the following opinions were put forward: (A) Regarding the ordinary budget: (1) It was found that the new income for 1933, excluding the land price tax of 1.5 million yuan and the Shatien government property income of 300,000 yuan, totaling 1.8 million yuan, the remaining tax revenues all had the possibility of gradual increase. However, without the actual income figures from the previous year or the year before for reference, it was difficult to review whether these planned figures were for the purpose of increasing revenue due to inflated expenditures. (2) Expenditures for various expenses in 1933 have increased. Apart from debt expenses due to special circumstances, are there any concrete plans for the various projects that should be carried out this year? Based on the superficial view of the proposed estimates, apart from public security expenses due to the approved additional budget, if other expenses such as those that can be separately slowed down and reduced can be separately tightened, then public funds can be saved from being wasted. (3) In order to prevent revenue shortages and to ensure that the budget revenue and expenditure are suitable, expenditures should be reduced and the income from new revenue items should be used to prepare for municipal prosperity reserve funds. It would be appropriate to increase the amount in proportion to ensure the safety of the city's financial operations. (B) Regarding the operating budget: (1) It was found that the pure profit income of the city's bank was not listed in either the ordinary budget or the operating budget. The reason for this is unknown. 2. The budget deficit of 286,920 yuan in 1933 should be planned and compensated for in some way, but this was not mentioned. After yesterday's meeting, it was decided that since the financial statements for 1931 and 1932 had special circumstances and had not yet been compiled, the actual revenue and expenditure of the Municipal Government and its affiliated agencies in that year should have records that could be checked. Therefore, the Municipal Government was still requested to send the actual revenue and expenditure records for those two years to the Council as soon as possible for budget review.

Rebuilding Disaster Areas

Since its establishment, the Municipal Council considered its greatest tasks to be (1) reviewing budgets and financial statements and (2) rebuilding disaster areas. The former is related to the burden on citizens and whether the use of funds is appropriate, and it is also related to the rise and fall of municipal administration. The latter, rebuilding the war zones, is to revitalize the city's appearance and also to seek welfare for the citizens. However, the issuance of reconstruction bonds was before the establishment of the Council, and the Council should supervise the use of the reconstruction bonds after the fact. Therefore, immediately after its establishment, it sent a letter to the Municipal Government, requesting that the entire case of the issuance of reconstruction bonds be sent to the Council. Because the matter was important, a disaster area reconstruction team was specially set up to handle it. After reviewing the case, the team found that, according to the original plan, the Municipal Government had transferred 37.49% of the funds for other uses, that is, 800,000 yuan for building public houses in Zhabei, Jiangwan, and Wusong, for building municipal government and bureau buildings in the city center, and 1 million yuan earmarked for lending to small business owners in war zones such as Zhabei, Jiangwan, and Wusong to rebuild their houses, for the Municipal Government to open a trust department. According to the recent income and expenditure statement of the Shanghai Reconstruction Bonds distributed by the Municipal Government representatives at the meeting at that time, the actual expenditure for repairing bridges and roads in the war zones of Zhabei, Wusong, and Jiangwan was only 50,000 yuan, which was only 1/20 of the quota of 1 million yuan. It can be seen from this whether or not efforts have been made for reconstruction work. Immediately afterward, the Municipal Government was asked to quickly explain what it would do for the disaster area reconstruction project, and to send the entire implementation plan and remedial measures to the Council for discussion. The Municipal Government replied that transferring the funds for building public houses in Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong, and other districts to build municipal government buildings in the city center was not a change of purpose. Furthermore, increasing the capital of the Municipal Bank to start a trust business was originally to meet the needs of small business owners and others in the disaster areas after the war to borrow money to rebuild houses, which was part of the post-war relief efforts. As for the engineering aspects, the ditches in Wusong and Jiangwan districts have been completed, and 80% of the roads have been completed. In the Zhabei district, in addition to Jiaotong Road, bridges such as Qingyun Bridge, Tiantong'an Bridge, Qiujiang Road Bridge, and Bazhi Bridge have all been completed. The restoration of the embankment on Guangfu Road, as well as the Linping Road Bridge and Tiantong Road Bridge in the Yinxiang district, have also been completed. It was heard that at the meeting, the disaster area reconstruction team believed that what was recovered was still not satisfactory. The main points were: (1) The Municipal Government's expenses for building houses and other expenses have already reached 500,000 yuan in municipal bonds, which must have been used for the purpose for which they were originally designated. If it is intended to increase embellishments, resulting in a lack of funds, then without the fundraising of reconstruction bonds, will the Municipal Government issue new bonds to complete this construction? (2) The canals for roads in the city center have been entirely borne by the households in the concession area, otherwise the land that was confiscated at a penalty of several hundred yuan will be requisitioned for several thousand yuan. (3) The Municipal Government's use of a huge sum of 1.3 million yuan to build the Municipal Government and bureau buildings in the city center raises the question of whether the post-disaster construction projects in the disaster areas are not more urgent than this. As for transferring the loans for rebuilding houses destroyed by small business owners in Zhabei and Jiangwan to the trust department, it should also be listed as a loan entrusted to the Municipal Bank and should not be listed as adding capital to the Municipal Bank. Furthermore, it should be specified whether it was designated at the time of allocation, whether a public announcement was made, when it started to be handled, and what the results of the handling were. Also, the work of tidying up roads and ditches in the disaster areas should be carried out in accordance with the original plan, and the extent of the work should be clarified. Even without the occurrence of disasters, roads, bridges, and ditches would have to be repaired and tidied up every year, so the Municipal Government is still asked to give a detailed reply to share the information with the citizens. All of this was passed at the meeting and forwarded to the Municipal Government for verification and reply.

General Resignation

The Provisional Municipal Council of this city was established on October 16 of last year. According to the provisions of Article 3 of the Council's Organizational Regulations, its term of office should last until the establishment of the Municipal Council (i.e., the elected one). However, the councilors believed that the term of office should be limited, so at the time of the inaugural meeting, they themselves declared that it would be for one year. Now it is about to expire, so at yesterday's meeting, a motion was made for general resignation, which was unanimously agreed upon by all present. In addition, several other cases were discussed, such as the referral of the land price tax case for review and the revision of the regulations of the Security Committee.
